  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c63ae49c-fe4a-4597-bff0-ff2d9554787b'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16674263171361930859">Every year, the people of the Protectorate leave a baby as an offering to the witch who lives in the forest. They hope this sacrifice will keep her from terrorizing their town. But the witch in the forest, Xan, is kind and gentle. She shares her home with a wise Swamp Monster named Glerk and a Perfectly Tiny Dragon, Fyrian. Xan rescues the abandoned children and deliver th</span>
  <span id="freeText16674263171361930859" style="display:none">Every year, the people of the Protectorate leave a baby as an offering to the witch who lives in the forest. They hope this sacrifice will keep her from terrorizing their town. But the witch in the forest, Xan, is kind and gentle. She shares her home with a wise Swamp Monster named Glerk and a Perfectly Tiny Dragon, Fyrian. Xan rescues the abandoned children and deliver them to welcoming families on the other side of the forest, nourishing the babies with starlight on the journey. <br /><br /> One year, Xan accidentally feeds a baby moonlight instead of starlight, filling the ordinary child with extraordinary magic. Xan decides she must raise this enmagicked girl, whom she calls Luna, as her own. To keep young Luna safe from her own unwieldy power, Xan locks her magic deep inside her. When Luna approaches her thirteenth birthday, her magic begins to emerge on schedule--but Xan is far away. Meanwhile, a young man from the Protectorate is determined to free his people by killing the witch. Soon, it is up to Luna to protect those who have protected her--even if it means the end of the loving, safe world she’s always known.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16674263171361930859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_818797'><a id="like_count_community_question_818797" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/818797?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">32 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28110852-the-girl-who-drank-the-moon">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/35524326-kelly"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1564052449i/35524326._UX100_CR0,12,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/35524326-kelly">Kelly</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I wrote this with a fifth grade reader in mind - but the cool thing about Middle Grade Fiction in general is that it allows for "Big Tent Storytelling<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I wrote this with a fifth grade reader in mind - but the cool thing about Middle Grade Fiction in general is that it allows for "Big Tent Storytelling". In other words, everyone is invited: little kids, big kids, teenagers, adults, old people. Everyone. The story manifests differently for different people - just like my experience reading THE LION, THE WITCH AND THE WARDROBE as an adult is different than the experience I had as a teenager, which is different than the experience I had as a child. Same book, different stories. There are some scary bits in this story, but no scarier than any other fairy tale. If they can handle the prose (and I don't pull any punches with the difficulty; I always expect my readers to come with their A game), then they can handle the content. I hope that helps!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1016138-hi-question--is-the-girl-herself-or-an">Hi! Question- is the Girl herself (or an of the other characters- excluding the dragons-) from a more diverse (or at least non-white) background? The girl on the cover looks like she might be of Hispanic or Latino background. Was it ever mentioned in the book? Hoping the answer is yes!</a>
</div>

<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/9028848-mary-lanham"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1337964579i/9028848._UY100_CR8,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/9028848-mary-lanham">Mary Lanham</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The book doesn't include real-world ethnicities or races, but several of the main characters are described as having darker skin and curling black hai<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The book doesn't include real-world ethnicities or races, but several of the main characters are described as having darker skin and curling black hair. The setting has a classic fairy tale feel without being overtly European, so it's the sort of book kids from many different backgrounds will be able to identify with. Hope this is helpful!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_1938963210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1938963210" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1938963210?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=newbery-winner">newbery-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1938963210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6257995203495908486"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_ohl33SghDI' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/kJU80vT' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508772917i/24252968._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The people of the Protectorate leave a baby deep in the forest each year, a sacrificial offering made to a witch to deter her from terrorizing the village. When the witch, Xan, finds the babies, she feeds them starlight, but one year she accidentally pulls light from the moon and <i>enmagicks</i> a baby girl. Xan knows that the baby imbued with moonlight will have extraordinary abilities, so she decides to rais</span>
  <span id="freeText6257995203495908486" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_ohl33SghDI" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/kJU80vT" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508772917i/24252968._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The people of the Protectorate leave a baby deep in the forest each year, a sacrificial offering made to a witch to deter her from terrorizing the village. When the witch, Xan, finds the babies, she feeds them starlight, but one year she accidentally pulls light from the moon and <i>enmagicks</i> a baby girl. Xan knows that the baby imbued with moonlight will have extraordinary abilities, so she decides to raise the child. As the child grows, she lacks the skill to control her evermore erratic magic, and her thirteenth birthday approaches - a day when her magic threatens to emerge in full and with dangerous consequences. <br><br><i>The Girl Who Drank the Moon</i> is a shining example of a good ol' fashioned fairy tale, replete with witches and dragons and creatures from the bog, along with enchanted objects, talking animals, and villainous monsters. <br><br>The setting is moody and atmospheric, be it the fog-riddled village populated with sorrowful people or the treacherous forest said to have taken the lives of travelers who stumbled into its boiling streams or choked on the foul-smelling fumes spewed from its fissures. <br><br><i>Fog clung to the city walls and cobbled streets like tenacious moss.</i> <br><br><i>At the center of the forest was a small swamp - bubbly, sulfury, and noxious, fed and warmed by an underground, restlessly sleeping volcano and covered with a slick of slime whose color ranged from poison green to lightning blue to blood red, depending on the time of year.</i> <br><br>Because this is a multigenerational saga, the cast of characters is relatively large, but each character brings their own quirks and idiosyncrasies to the page, making them easy to differentiate (though pinpointing a "main character" is a bit of a grey area). <br><br>The best part of the book - the succulent cherry on top of this decadent treat - is the way magic is used or emerges by accident. Magic is portrayed as being whimsical and sweet, familiar yet fresh. Some forms of magic are playful in their innocence, while other forms rely on the exchange of a sinister currency that is disturbing to read about whenever it's employed. <br><br><i>She transformed a book into a dove and enlivened her pencils and quills so that they stood on their own and performed a complicated dance on the desk.</i> <br><br><i>As [she] ran, each footstep blossomed with iridescent flowers. When she waded into the swamp, the reeds twisted themselves into a boat, and she climbed aboard, floating across the deep red of algae coating the water.</i> <br><br>The story is fairly complicated for a middle grade novel and some elements are disquieting; the book is subsequently recommended for a slightly older audience (ages 10 to 14). <br><br>With luscious prose, a winding plot, and a charming cast of characters, <i>The Girl Who Drank the Moon</i> makes a proud addition to the list of Newbery Medal winners. <br>- <br>This book will likely appeal to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/150739.Dealing_with_Dragons?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">The Enchanted Forest Chronicles</a> by Patricia C. Wrede, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22833921-the-mermaid-s-sister?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mermaid's Sister</a> by Carrie Anne Noble, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16793.Stardust?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Stardust</a> by Neil Gaiman.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6257995203495908486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1797001184" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1797001184" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1797001184?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1797001184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8610337131762673068">4 1/2 stars.<br/><br/>This is the story of a little baby girl sent to die but who is adopted by a good witch instead. Without meaning to, the Witch pours magic into Luna but, instead of letting her draw from her magic, she bounds it until Luna’s thirteenth birthday.<br/><br/>Incidentally, that is the day the Witch decides to let herself die. But that day is coming and coming, closer and closer, and the Witch starts to regret her decision.<br/><br/>There obviously is more happening in the story than only that. In fact, we hav</span>
  <span id="freeText8610337131762673068" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars.<br /><br />This is the story of a little baby girl sent to die but who is adopted by a good witch instead. Without meaning to, the Witch pours magic into Luna but, instead of letting her draw from her magic, she bounds it until Luna’s thirteenth birthday.<br /><br />Incidentally, that is the day the Witch decides to let herself die. But that day is coming and coming, closer and closer, and the Witch starts to regret her decision.<br /><br />There obviously is more happening in the story than only that. In fact, we have points of view specific to a variety of characters and even two dragons! But summarizing would take too much space, when what I really want to do is praise this book for its magnificent content.<br /><br />Oh, what a magical writing style. It’s so lyrical, so memorable, so sense-awakening. Definitely suited for a middle grade novel, while being interesting and original enough to hold even an adult’s attention or someone who is not entirely into books for kids. We need voices in literature that have their own different style, and Kelly Barnhill is a refreshing one.<br /><br />There is a lovely fairytale-esque atmosphere in the story that made me want to read this aloud to children in my community. Any book that provokes this reaction is worth a good hand of applause! This book also made me feel astoundingly empathic to the Witch, whom is such a caring, misjudged creature. Oh, oh, I must not forget to mention that the little dragon Fyrian is exactly like… Well, you remember Mulan’s quirky, hilarious dragon companion? Yeah, that’s Fyrian alright.<br /><br />In a perfect world, every kid would have read this enchanting story.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8610337131762673068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1711512309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711512309" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25478105-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462374579p2/25478105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711512309?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/25478105-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29417336-the-girl-who-drank-the-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711512309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9512458857158559572">Look at that beaut' of a cover guys! How could anyone walk past this in a bookstore and <em>NOT</em> want to read it?! And then the blurb: witches, tiny dragons, swamp monsters, lunar magic...this book had all the ingredients for me to drop everything and just <em>read</em>! Which is why it turned out to be even more disappointing than it would've been without the great expectations...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472646003i/20220169._SX540_.jpg' alt='Blurb (8)' width='600' height='74' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oh, where to start?! The first 10% was fabulous. After that:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472646003ra/20220170.gif' alt='giphy (3).gif' width='383' height='255' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'll just divide this review into pros and cons to make it easier for </span>
  <span id="freeText9512458857158559572" style="display:none">Look at that beaut' of a cover guys! How could anyone walk past this in a bookstore and <em>NOT</em> want to read it?! And then the blurb: witches, tiny dragons, swamp monsters, lunar magic...this book had all the ingredients for me to drop everything and just <em>read</em>! Which is why it turned out to be even more disappointing than it would've been without the great expectations...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472646003i/20220169._SX540_.jpg" alt="Blurb (8)" width="600" height="74" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, where to start?! The first 10% was fabulous. After that:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472646003ra/20220170.gif" alt="giphy (3).gif" width="383" height="255" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll just divide this review into pros and cons to make it easier for me to keep it organised and easier for you to read it!<br><br><strong>The Pros:</strong><br><br>- Magic being drawn directly from mother nature.<br><br>- There are a lot of strong female characters present.<br><br>- You can discover several elements from classic fairy tales such as Hansel and Gretel, and Little Thumbling.<br><br>- Glerk, the friendly gross-looking Swamp Monster. Who doesn't want a scary looking monster for a friend? It's the entire reason I'm the proud owner of an Old English Bulldog!<br><br>- Fyrian, the tiny naive dragon with ADD. He reminded me of the original Toothless a lot and we 'all' know how much I love <em>him</em>! <a href="http://strixmoonwing.deviantart.com/art/Toothless-vs-Toothless-164549155" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472646003i/20220171._SX540_.jpg" alt="toothless" width="358" height="260" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><strong>The Cons:</strong><br>- The repetitiveness of the story. One of my Kindle notes on this said:<br><br>"<em>If I have to read about Luna's magic seeping out of her pores one more time, I'll eat my fucking sock</em>."<br><br>- The magical realism. If I read a fairytale, I want it to be a 100% fairytale and with none of that emotional metaphorical nonsense.<br><br>- The length of the book. It could have easily been cut by a 100 pages if you take out all the redundant parts.<br><br>-This is supposedly Middle-Grade fiction, but I found it a bit too dark for that at times. <em>Especially</em> in combination with the magical realism. No 10-year-old wants to read about depressed grownups being drowned in magical sorrow. I'm aware that most of the classic myths and fairy tales are also quite dark and have lots of metaphors in them. Yet it's all about being subtle, which wasn't the case in <em>The Girl Who Drank the Moon</em>.<br><br>-The male characters are depicted as ignorant simpletons. Which, as a self-proclaimed feminist, shouldn't be that much of a problem *winks*, but I like to see a certain balance between the genders.<br><br>-The story tends to drag on and on. I had a hard time ploughing through it at the end.<br><br><strong>TL; DR: </strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472646003ra/20220172.gif" alt="giphy (4).gif" width="271" height="193" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The concept is nice. Combining nature with magic and weaving it into a fairy tale is fantastic. Sadly, it was poorly executed in this one. I'm giving it two brownies, meaning it was okay. I'd really like to see a properly edited version some day, though!<br>Not really recommending it. However, if you're a big fan of magical realism, you might be able to appreciate this book a lot more than I did.<br><br><em>Thanks to Algonquin Young Readers for providing me with a copy via NetGalley in exchange for an honest opinion!</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="9512458857158559572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2772890653" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2772890653" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2772890653?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2772890653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5673204132573987595">Winner of the 2017 Newbery Medal<br/>An Entertainment Weekly Best Middle Grade Book of 2016<br/>A New York Public Library Best Book of 2016<br/>A Chicago Public Library Best Book of 2016<br/>An Amazon Top 20 Best Book of 2016<br/>A Publishers Weekly Best Book of 2016<br/>A School Library Journal Best Book of 2016<br/>Named to KirkusReviews’ Best Books of 2016<br/>2017 Booklist Youth Editors’ Choice<br/><br/><br/>So, this book has won a lot of awards and it is easy to see why. This is a great book for middle school readers who enjoy some fantasy and </span>
  <span id="freeText5673204132573987595" style="display:none">Winner of the 2017 Newbery Medal<br />An Entertainment Weekly Best Middle Grade Book of 2016<br />A New York Public Library Best Book of 2016<br />A Chicago Public Library Best Book of 2016<br />An Amazon Top 20 Best Book of 2016<br />A Publishers Weekly Best Book of 2016<br />A School Library Journal Best Book of 2016<br />Named to KirkusReviews’ Best Books of 2016<br />2017 Booklist Youth Editors’ Choice<br /><br /><br />So, this book has won a lot of awards and it is easy to see why. This is a great book for middle school readers who enjoy some fantasy and supernatural elements in their books. Plus, the writing is beautiful, lyrical even at times. It really gives the feel of being in a fairy tale land where every year the people of the Protectorate give up an infant to the witch in the forest. They believe abandoning a child (i.e. sacrificing the baby) will protect them from the *gasp* wicked witch who lives there.<br /><br />Every year, Xan, rescues the abandoned children in the forest. She is a kind and loving witch. She doesn't understand why the people would leave their infants in the forest. She cuddles them, nourishes them with starlight and finds them new homes with loving families on the other side of the forest. Xan lives with a miniature dragon and a clever swamp monster. She is quite content and one evening she rescues a baby and accidentally gives her moonlight instead of starlight. OOPS! That's a big no-no. So, Xan decides to raise the girl as her own and names her Luna. As Luna draws near her thirteenth birthday and her magic begins to show, things begin to happen....<br /><br />So obviously there is magic in this book but there was for me also nice messages about loyalty, family and what makes a family. That family can be the family one is born into, but it is also the family we choose, those we let in and share our lives with. It's about learning the truth, coming home, and what is truly magical. This book also has some bittersweet moments because it is also about saying goodbye, about loss, and about grief. What is sorrow? What is sadness? How do we cope with these emotions?<br /><br />The characters are quirky, like-able - and yes, lovable. A witch raising a child in the woods, what is so magical about that??? Everything! Keep in mind this was written for middle grade readers and it is geared for the age range but don't let that stop you. If you have a middle school reader, this would be a great book to read with your child as there are a lot of relevant issues in this book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5673204132573987595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.K. Gold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.K. Gold" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold">R.K. Gold</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677676554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1600439662195388706">Update: 3-3.5 stars I really didn’t feel comfortable giving this book 4 stars. I have a lot of friends who LOVED this book and I really wanted to love it too but just couldn’t. I didn’t dislike this book, there was some beautiful writing in it, but I can’t bring myself to rate it any higher. <br/>———<br/>some minor spoilers ahead It started slow for me and I was terrified I was going to not enjoy this book. A lot of my friends recommended it, and all wrote glowing reviews. It sounded right up my alley. I </span>
  <span id="freeText1600439662195388706" style="display:none">Update: 3-3.5 stars I really didn’t feel comfortable giving this book 4 stars. I have a lot of friends who LOVED this book and I really wanted to love it too but just couldn’t. I didn’t dislike this book, there was some beautiful writing in it, but I can’t bring myself to rate it any higher. <br />———<br />some minor spoilers ahead It started slow for me and I was terrified I was going to not enjoy this book. A lot of my friends recommended it, and all wrote glowing reviews. It sounded right up my alley. I love whimsical tales that leave me in wonder and the first 65% of the book had some breathtaking descriptions including a memorable description of a dragon underbelly the color of a freshly laid egg, however the pace was too slow—13 years passed and nothing happened. I fully expected to give this book a 2.5-3 star rating until the real journey began—once Amun’s started her journey of magical discovery and Xan started her rapid aging, the pacing picked up and a clear clock began to tick towards the climax. The final 35% of the book was a solid 5 star read with a beautiful ending that left a smile on my face.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1743852816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14101779000750465796">This is a new favorite book of mine. I love this book. I love Luna and her dragon. I love the witch who feed her moonlight. The story feels so big and it seems there is more to it and behind it. I love the tone of the book and the feeling of magic conveyed to the reader. There are some really horrible things that happen in the village and Sister Igraine is quite a character. I love the resolution of the book and how things conclude. It is so satisfying. I don't want to give anything away, simply</span>
  <span id="freeText14101779000750465796" style="display:none">This is a new favorite book of mine. I love this book. I love Luna and her dragon. I love the witch who feed her moonlight. The story feels so big and it seems there is more to it and behind it. I love the tone of the book and the feeling of magic conveyed to the reader. There are some really horrible things that happen in the village and Sister Igraine is quite a character. I love the resolution of the book and how things conclude. It is so satisfying. I don't want to give anything away, simply read the story as it's worth your time. <br /><br />I love the prose of this work. It is beautiful and it's like a spindle thread of a spider web that has collected the nights dew and now sparkles like diamonds in the sun. Such a work of beauty. I have so enjoyed reading this book and I will miss being part of it's world. This would be one of my favorite books of 2017 for me. It more than deserves the Newberry award.<br /><br />This book deals with belonging, of life and death, growing up and loss. It deals with sorrow. It turns all this to magic, to transformation and growth. This is a STORY!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9790601043192503481">4.5 stars<br/><br/>A beautiful, surprisingly complex story. Perhaps it is a little longer with somewhat darker themes than many middle grade books, but that's not necessarily a bad thing. This reminded me in some ways of A Wrinkle in Time -- the author didn't pull any punches when it came to more sensitive subjects like grief and death. <br/><br/>Although this book deals with some pretty heavy topics, there is also humour sprinkled throughout that lightens the tone.   <span id="freeText9790601043192503481" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />A beautiful, surprisingly complex story. Perhaps it is a little longer with somewhat darker themes than many middle grade books, but that's not necessarily a bad thing. This reminded me in some ways of A Wrinkle in Time -- the author didn't pull any punches when it came to more sensitive subjects like grief and death. <br /><br />Although this book deals with some pretty heavy topics, there is also humour sprinkled throughout that lightens the tone. I listened to the audible edition, and Christina Moore did a fantastic job with the various voices.<br /><br />Badass Female Character score: 5/5 -- At its heart, this is a story about the strength of women. From Xan, to Luna, to the women in the village, this book is filled with women and how they use the powers they possess.</span>

<div id="review_1730662797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730662797" />
    <a title="Renata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/697616-renata"><img alt="Renata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390698658p2/697616.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730662797?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renata" href="/user/show/697616-renata">Renata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/697616-renata?shelf=children-s-and-ya-lit">children-s-and-ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730662797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1938953533990673741">The beauty of this book begins with its magical title: The Girl Who Drank the Moon. <br/>Luna is enmagicked as a baby by being fed the silvery honeyed moon beams. I was both jealous of that experience and yet felt kinship with it - how often have I felt graced by the gentle silvery radiance of moonlight! Of course, this being a fantasy novel,Luna's magic was more tangible!<br/> The Girl Who Drank the Moon is a fabulous work of fantasy pulling strongly on the art of storytelling and richly imbued with inte</span>
  <span id="freeText1938953533990673741" style="display:none">The beauty of this book begins with its magical title: The Girl Who Drank the Moon. <br />Luna is enmagicked as a baby by being fed the silvery honeyed moon beams. I was both jealous of that experience and yet felt kinship with it - how often have I felt graced by the gentle silvery radiance of moonlight! Of course, this being a fantasy novel,Luna's magic was more tangible!<br /> The Girl Who Drank the Moon is a fabulous work of fantasy pulling strongly on the art of storytelling and richly imbued with interesting characters and an unusually imaginative setting.<br /> Of course we have the deep, dark forest home to dangers real and imagined.<br />There is an enormous bog surrounding the Protectorate (ironically named) which poses many dangers to the villagers and from which they eek out a mere subsistence livelihood. But there is also an immense volcanic area surrounding this all with treacherous vents, steaming cauldrons of gasses and seven craters marking the border -it kept putting images of Yellowstone in my mind.<br /> After the beginning event, the story unfolds slowly and it is a leisurely exploration of two separate plot threads. One is the life in the Protectorate where villagers have an appalling tradition of offering a young baby to the witch in the woods. All this happens in the first few pages, so no spoiler here. We meet the young ANTAIN whose uncle is a powerful Elder. We quickly realize ANTAIN is a kind and sensitive soul. We know he will be a good character, perhaps a hero but perhaps just an innocent who in fairy tale fashion will gather goodness to him. His is a wonderfully developed character - much richer than I would have expected.<br /> Naturally we have a witch (or two or three) and Xan, our main character, is an unexpected delight. Loved that she is the antithesis of usual witches. And then there are the unique creatures of the fantasy world: Fyrian, a miniature rainbow colored dragon who is all love and enthusiasm and naïveté - and just wants everyone to get along. Even though he had mysteries about him he provides a kind of childlike delightful humor. <br /> My favorite creature is Glerk, the poetic monster of the Bog who may have five or six legs and a prehensile tail and is long time loyal friend to Xan and protector of Fyrian and young Luna. Glerk , the great poet of the Bog: "In the beginning, there was only Bog, and Bog, and Bog. The Bog was everything, and everything was the Bog. <br /> But the Bog was lonely. It wanted eyes with which to see the world. It wanted a strong back with which to carry itself from place to place. It wanted legs to walk and hands to touch and a mouth that could sing.<br /> And so the Bog created a Body: a great Beast that walked out of the Bog on its own strong boggy legs. The Beast was the Bog and the Bog was the Beast. The Beast lived the Bog and the Bog loved the Beast, just as a person loves the image of himself in a quiet pond of water, and looks upon it with tenderness. The Beasts chest was full of warm and life-giving compassion. He felt the shine of love radiating outward. And the Beast wanted words to explain how he felt. ...He opened his mouth and a poem came out."<br /> This is not a traditional quest story. It's a story about secrets that can do harm, about misguided protection, about young people needing to grow up to be their true self, about the beauty and pain of motherly love, about the cost of sorrow and healing power of hope. It's beautifully told - such gorgeous writing. It radiates love - but it would not be balanced without some villains.<br /> "Time was a tricky thing - as slippery as mud" - a refrain throughout the book. When is it time to tell young people true things, when does protecting them deny them power over their own life, when is it time to teach the important things they need to know to empower them. <br /> It's a beautiful story - perfect as a read aloud/read together for eight to nine year olds, (course I would argue longer but I'm always keen on shared reading for the way discussions can grow with your kids) and certainly independent reading from nine on up. I did shed some tears at the end - a heartwarming read! As my granddaughter said, "Nana, there is a sad part at the end, but don't worry - it's a good kind of sad."</span>
  <a data-text-id="1938953533990673741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1602698448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602698448" />
    <a title="La La" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17265997-la-la"><img alt="La La" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468213406p2/17265997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1602698448?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="La La" class="user" itemprop="url" name="La La" href="/user/show/17265997-la-la">La La</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29417336-the-girl-who-drank-the-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17265997-la-la?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17265997-la-la?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17265997-la-la?shelf=review-arcs-netgalley">review-arcs-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602698448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4938799175326256662">This book was way too long for Middle Grade, there was too much boring political content, and it was having a huge identity crisis. Some parts read like a great Children's chapterbook, a lot of it was based on an older character and read like okay YA, and then there were two adults in the story who had their adult thinking added in too often. For such a long book there was very little MG age interesting content.<br/><br/>Many of the scenes were too long and a lot of them were basically the same scene in a</span>
  <span id="freeText4938799175326256662" style="display:none">This book was way too long for Middle Grade, there was too much boring political content, and it was having a huge identity crisis. Some parts read like a great Children's chapterbook, a lot of it was based on an older character and read like okay YA, and then there were two adults in the story who had their adult thinking added in too often. For such a long book there was very little MG age interesting content.<br /><br />Many of the scenes were too long and a lot of them were basically the same scene in a different location. It would have been better to write things like, "She felt like she did the day she found the *fill in the blank* when she picked up the book," instead of describing the same sensations and thoughts over, and over, and over again. If these redundant scenes had been taken out, and most of the adult storyline extracted, the book would have been more MG length and a lot more interesting for MG age readers.<br /><br />Luna, the bog monster, and the tiny dragon were the highlights of the story and more focus should have been on them. This book needed an editor who knows MG inside and out. I was excited to read this book after reading the summary, but ended up being disappointed.<br /><br />I was approved for an eARC, via Netgalley, in return for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4938799175326256662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2021408482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021408482" />
    <a title="Book Riot Community" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33447134-book-riot-community"><img alt="Book Riot Community" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583162430p2/33447134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021408482?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Riot Community" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Riot Community" href="/user/show/33447134-book-riot-community">Book Riot Community</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021408482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11919442973207865738">I’m not surprised this won the Newbery, because it is absolutely stunning. Told in a wonderfully mystical narrative, this book is sure to join the ranks of enduring middle grade classics. The story centers around a long held tradition in the Protectorate, that every year the youngest child must be sacrificed to appease the witch in the forest. But right away the reader finds out the the witch, named Xan, is actually kind and makes the yearly trek to the Protectorate to save the babies from dying</span>
  <span id="freeText11919442973207865738" style="display:none">I’m not surprised this won the Newbery, because it is absolutely stunning. Told in a wonderfully mystical narrative, this book is sure to join the ranks of enduring middle grade classics. The story centers around a long held tradition in the Protectorate, that every year the youngest child must be sacrificed to appease the witch in the forest. But right away the reader finds out the the witch, named Xan, is actually kind and makes the yearly trek to the Protectorate to save the babies from dying alone. One day, Xan picks up a baby girl and instead of feeding her starlight she feeds her moonlight, which imbues the child with incredible powers. What follows is an intricate cast of characters that are all affected by Luna, the girl who drank the moon. I loved every word in this book, and I look forward to reading it again and again and again.<br /><br />–Karina Glaser<br /><br /><br />from The Best Books We Read In March 2017: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookriot.com/2017/04/04/riot-roundup-best-books-read-march/">http://bookriot.com/2017/04/04/riot-r...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11919442973207865738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1901925731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1901925731" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5276440-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515385385p2/5276440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1901925731?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/5276440-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1901925731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11770508857570501110">Fwew. Finally! It felt like it took me forever to finally get through this. I would rate this somewhere between 3 and 3.5 stars. It's not a bad book, but for a Newbery winner, I was expecting more.<br/><br/>What Worked:<br/><br/>The writing is very pretty. Descriptive, poetic, lyrical...it has all the makings of an old-fashioned fairy tale story. <br/><br/>It has some intriguing characters- a swamp monster who's been around since the beginning of the world, a sorrow eater, a childlike dragon, a magical girl...it has a lot of</span>
  <span id="freeText11770508857570501110" style="display:none">Fwew. Finally! It felt like it took me forever to finally get through this. I would rate this somewhere between 3 and 3.5 stars. It's not a bad book, but for a Newbery winner, I was expecting more.<br /><br />What Worked:<br /><br />The writing is very pretty. Descriptive, poetic, lyrical...it has all the makings of an old-fashioned fairy tale story. <br /><br />It has some intriguing characters- a swamp monster who's been around since the beginning of the world, a sorrow eater, a childlike dragon, a magical girl...it has a lot of promise.<br /><br />What Didn't Work for Me:<br /><br />This was slow. It's a case of lots of description and showing and not much action actually happening. It's quite passive. Sleepy would be the word I would use to describe the plot. 13 years go by in the book, but hardly anything really...happens. The first 2/3 sets up the events of the last third of the book, constantly hinting at things to come. And then it does come...and everything fits together seamlessly. There's no real tension or showdown or anything to make the reader wonder what the outcome will be. The climax is a bunch of characters finally meeting, the villain losing without a fight, and a natural disaster that doesn't end up threatening any lives or much besides Xan's home. If you like excitement, there isn't much here.<br /><br />The writing gets repetitive. Ideas such as the bog, magic being locked inside Luna, poetry, etc. are discussed over and over again. "She is here", "Sorrow is dangerous"...I feel like some ideas and themes were beaten to death. Sometimes the description was so...descriptive that I lost interest and went foggy, having to re-read entire pages. This is so full of symbolic imagery and poetic figurative language that the plot gets a big lost in it. Problem is, I didn't always know what it was getting at. What was up with the bog? Is it symbolic for life? Death? Both? All of the paper birds...was that about the Madwoman trying to fly to her child? Why did they cut up Antain's face? Why was Fyrian small for years and suddenly large? Was he linked with Luna? I could have used a bit more concrete information.<br /><br />Examples: "She was an old woman. She was a girl. She was somewhere in between. She was all of those things at once." Huh?<br /><br />"In the beginning, there was the bog. And the bog covered the world and the Bog was the world and the world was the Bog." WTF (This is mentioned several times throughout the story. I still don't get it.)<br /><br />The POV can be a bit confusing. There are a ton of characters- Xan, Glerk, Fyrian, Luna, the Madwoman, Antain, Grand Elder Gherland, Ethyne- that at some point or another become the focus for the omniscient narrator. It's a lot. And when most of these characters come together and start speaking to each other, the pronouns could have been a bit better defined, IMO. There are also short "story" chapters, in some of which I'm not exactly sure who is supposed to be speaking. Some of the characters' musings get off topic and go on for too long. I feel like this could have been about 100 pages shorter cleaned up. <br /><br /><br />So...This is okay. Not bad, but not award-winning IMO. Also, it's supposedly written with 5th graders in mind. I teach fifth grade language arts, and I don't think most of my kids would "get this" and want to stick with it. It's like a middle grades book that middle grades kids would be bored by. I think that Diana Wynne Jones or Neil Gaiman has written in a similar vein, but better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11770508857570501110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iryna *Book and Sword*" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword">Iryna *Book and Sword*</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword?shelf=from-the-library">from-the-library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1902679234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11573272209932967745"><b>pre-read </b><br/>This has been on my TBR for awhile, and I have finally checked out a copy from the library.<br/>For some reason I have a feeling that I will love it. <br/>Just have to finish some other books first. <br/>___________________________________<br/><br/><b>“Not all knowledge comes from the mind. Your body, your heart, your intuition. Sometimes memories even have minds of their own.”</b><br/><br/>For a book geared towards middle grade readers <b>The girl who drank the moon</b> is exceptionally wise. There were so many hidden truths in its m</span>
  <span id="freeText11573272209932967745" style="display:none"><b>pre-read </b><br />This has been on my TBR for awhile, and I have finally checked out a copy from the library.<br />For some reason I have a feeling that I will love it. <br />Just have to finish some other books first. <br />___________________________________<br /><br /><b>“Not all knowledge comes from the mind. Your body, your heart, your intuition. Sometimes memories even have minds of their own.”</b><br /><br />For a book geared towards middle grade readers <b>The girl who drank the moon</b> is exceptionally wise. There were so many hidden truths in its many quotable moments - I found myself taking my time with it. Trying to savor it.<br /><br />​I will say though that this book is probably not for everybody. It's quite different from other middle grade fantasy books - both in style of writing and structure.<br /><br />Some things would take a really long time to happen, and some other ones happen too quickly. Points of view jump and differ and wave through time, and stories and memories. To be completely honest I was quite confused for the first 100 pages or so. But somehow I was okay with that.<br /><br /><b>“And the more they asked, the more they wondered. And the more they wondered, the more they hoped. And the more they hoped, the more the clouds of sorrow lifted, drifted, and burned away in the heat of a brightening sky.”</b><br /><br />I would especially recommend this book to mothers, expectant mothers and families who are looking to adopt. The girl who drank the moon is bursting with motherly instincts, affection and family. And with love. So much love.<br /><br /><b>“Human babies are only tiny for an instant—their growing up is as swift as the beat of a hummingbird’s wing.”</b><br /><br />Kelly Barnhill really understands ​motherhood and growing up. She is either a fantastic mother herself, or knows somebody who is. The bonds of a child and a parent were so beautifully and vividly portrayed here, if anything that is enough of a reason to read this book.<br />I also really enjoyed the other aspect of the book, which focused on how some people abuse power and twists the truths to mold the reality they wish to impose. If I think about it, this book got quite political, but in a way that was accessible to younger readers.<br /><br /><b>“Knowledge is powerful, but it is a terrible power when it is hoarded and hidden.”</b><br /><br />A solid read with many beautiful messages, a definite must for young minds. As The girl who drank the moon tells that it's okay to grow up, that change is inevitable. It teaches to think for yourself and to question everything. It shows love for what it is - boundless, ever expanding and never jealous.<br /><br />I will definitely be reading more by this author in the near future.<br /><br /><b>“Everything you see is in the process of making or unmaking or dying or living. Everything is in a state of change.”</b><br /><br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book.and.sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">BOOKSTAGRAM</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_1907177880" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1907177880?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenny" href="/user/show/1642452-kenny">Kenny</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1907177880" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16038880419935676399">3.5/5<br/><br/><b><i>“Knowledge is power, but it is a terrible power when it is hoarded and hidden.”</i> <br/>― Kelly Barnhill, The Girl Who Drank the Moon</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533408821i/26077552._SX540_.jpg' alt='1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is a hard one for me to rate. I kept going back and forth between 3 or 4, and finally settled upon 3. There are things I loved about this book and other elements that I did not care for. This a book I really wanted to love and had high expectations for. Perhaps I've grown too old for YA novels.<br/><br/>An elderly witch, an enmagicked girl, a brave young father, a wise, po</span>
  <span id="freeText16038880419935676399" style="display:none">3.5/5<br><br><b><i>“Knowledge is power, but it is a terrible power when it is hoarded and hidden.”</i> <br>― Kelly Barnhill, The Girl Who Drank the Moon</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533408821i/26077552._SX540_.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a hard one for me to rate. I kept going back and forth between 3 or 4, and finally settled upon 3. There are things I loved about this book and other elements that I did not care for. This a book I really wanted to love and had high expectations for. Perhaps I've grown too old for YA novels.<br><br>An elderly witch, an enmagicked girl, a brave young father, a wise, poetry loving monster, a tiny dragon, with a huge heart, paper birds, and a mysterious madwoman meet to stop an evil witch who feeds on sorrow. The heroes and heroines here are all endearing; in fact they are enchanting. <br><br>As a baby, Luna is left as a sacrifical offering to an evil witch ~~ but is she??? Instead, the witch, Xan, rescues baby Luna, just as she had rescued hundred of babies like her the past 500 years. In addition to goat's milk, Xan feeds the babies starlight. That gives the babbies strength while Xan looks for a safe home for children. However, with Luna, Xan makes a huge mistake. She feeds Luna moonlight, which fills the girl with magical powers.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533408821i/26077551.png" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>As Luna grows, her magic is unstopable ~~ and truths begin to unfold about the place and her people and where she came from. There’s so much to love in this book ~~ and yet, I didn't love it. What I admire about <b>The Girl Who Drank the Moon</b> is Barnhill championing the spiritual powers of hope, love and rebellion in the face of fear and cruelty and nationalism. And while I didn't love this book, I do think it is is a marvelous read for young readers all over the world.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533408821i/26077553.jpg" alt="1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_3258782843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3258782843" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34465556-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588296669p2/34465556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3258782843?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/34465556-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=r-fantasy-bingo-2020">r-fantasy-bingo-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=owned-paperback">owned-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=newbery-medal">newbery-medal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=pub-2016">pub-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3258782843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13257538746549499995">In the Protectorate, a baby is sacrificed each year to the witch who lives in the forest to keep the peace. Or so the citizens believe. The witch is not wicked. She saves the babies and feeds them starlight, which causes them to have successful lives, and delivers them to a new, loving family in the Free Cities. The witch, Xan, lives with a monster named Glerk and a tiny dragon named Fyrian. When Xan accidentally feeds a baby moonlight, the baby is enmagicked, and Xan raises the child as her own</span>
  <span id="freeText13257538746549499995" style="display:none">In the Protectorate, a baby is sacrificed each year to the witch who lives in the forest to keep the peace. Or so the citizens believe. The witch is not wicked. She saves the babies and feeds them starlight, which causes them to have successful lives, and delivers them to a new, loving family in the Free Cities. The witch, Xan, lives with a monster named Glerk and a tiny dragon named Fyrian. When Xan accidentally feeds a baby moonlight, the baby is enmagicked, and Xan raises the child as her own, with Glerk and Fyrian to help. This eventually leads to trouble, as baby Luna grows into her magical abilities. Meanwhile, we also experience life in the Protectorate from the POV of a boy, Antain, who is supposed to join the Council of Elders and a women who went mad after being forced to give up her child. <br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 4.5</b><br /><br />The Girl Who Drank the Moon is extremely cute, often funny, and surprisingly dark for a middle grade novel. It’s about mothers and their children, and in fact the bond shared between all caregivers and their young charges. Many of the characters, including Antain, Luna, and Fyrian must grow up over the course of the novel. Thus, there are three coming-of-age stories hidden in one. It’s also nice that the parent figures aren’t perfect. Xan is not a perfect parent, and it makes her all the more lifelike and relatable. <br /><br />At just under 400 pages, this novel is somewhat long, but not too long. I was worried the large time span of the story—which ranges from Luna’s infancy to her thirteenth birthday—would make the story clunky, but my fears were unfounded. In fact, I could barely put this down until I had finished it. I was constantly worried for Xan, Luna, and the citizens of the Protectorate. Seeing them develop along the way was sweet and tender, and it gave the story breadth and feeling. <br /><br />This is a magical tale perfect for anyone of any age*, for everyone who has learned to love—as a parent, a child, or a friend. The story sucks you in until you finish, and you hear it’s message of love and hope loud and clear. <br /><br />*although perhaps too dark for children younger than 9 or 10</span>
  <a data-text-id="13257538746549499995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2020699057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2020699057" />
    <a title="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words"><img alt="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434161411p2/17825291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2020699057?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" href="/user/show/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words">Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2020699057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8537688415092683592">This book was a whimsical treasure of a book. It's one of those middle grade books that works on two levels, like a Pixar movie. Middle graders will love the story just for the story (even if some of the deeper themes woven in go over their head; not discounting children readers, though, we don't give them enough credit), but adults will also find a lot of deeper meaning to the book.<br/><br/> This is a story for EVERYONE to enjoy. <br/><br/>Beautiful writing, quirky, lovable characters (like a big-hearted and wise</span>
  <span id="freeText8537688415092683592" style="display:none">This book was a whimsical treasure of a book. It's one of those middle grade books that works on two levels, like a Pixar movie. Middle graders will love the story just for the story (even if some of the deeper themes woven in go over their head; not discounting children readers, though, we don't give them enough credit), but adults will also find a lot of deeper meaning to the book.<br /><br /> This is a story for EVERYONE to enjoy. <br /><br />Beautiful writing, quirky, lovable characters (like a big-hearted and wise swamp monster named Glerk, a delightful tiny dragon named Fyrian suffering from delusions of grandeur, and a sweet tempered and gentle witch named Xan), and most of all a plot that will make your heart grow bigger and bigger and bigger. It's ultimately about hope and forgiveness and love. Hope in the midst of suffering, forgiveness in the midst of failure, and loving so big and so much that no one is left out. And it's about consequences - the consequences of power unchecked, hiding from memories, and most of all, of pushing down and ignoring the hard things like sorrow and pain.<br /><br />I LOVED THIS BOOK. Please read it. Even if you never read middle grade. It's worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8537688415092683592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="i fall in love book blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog"><img alt="i fall in love book blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466826545p2/44022116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920784077?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="i fall in love book blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="i fall in love book blog" href="/user/show/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog">i fall in love book blog</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog?shelf=lonely">lonely</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog?shelf=no-raunch">no-raunch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog?shelf=sad-depressing-sad-sad-sad">sad-depressing-sad-sad-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44022116-i-fall-in-love-book-blog?shelf=atmosphere">atmosphere</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920784077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14814070610161364837">I've been done with this book for a couple of weeks, and wasn't sure how to write this review. I thought about just throwing a 3 or 4 star rating down and being done with it, but I feel like I owe it to my friends that have similar tastes to be honest. <br/><b>I wanted to love this book.</b> <br/>The cover was gorgeous.<br/>The writing was gorgeous.<br/>The ending came together perfectly.<br/><b>I didn't love this book.</b><br/> I kept pushing through it, hoping that I would have an "AH-HA" moment and fall head over heels in love with it.</span>
  <span id="freeText14814070610161364837" style="display:none">I've been done with this book for a couple of weeks, and wasn't sure how to write this review. I thought about just throwing a 3 or 4 star rating down and being done with it, but I feel like I owe it to my friends that have similar tastes to be honest. <br /><b>I wanted to love this book.</b> <br />The cover was gorgeous.<br />The writing was gorgeous.<br />The ending came together perfectly.<br /><b>I didn't love this book.</b><br /> I kept pushing through it, hoping that I would have an "AH-HA" moment and fall head over heels in love with it. I finished it, but kinda wish I hadn't wasted my time.<br />I don't see this as middle grade fiction. To me, it seems more like an adult book with a middle grade character. It's what adults <i>wished</i> middle graders wanted to read. The first 3/4 of the book is slow, sad and repetitive. I was bored. <br />It has so many elements that I thought I would love: A bog monster, a tiny dragon, and magic from the moon. All while living in a forest.<br />I wish it had worked for me.<br /><br />A tiny note for Audible listeners. The narrator for this book is FANTASTIC! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14814070610161364837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
