<div id="review_2352045186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352045186" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352045186?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352045186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17999708540913825445">This book was an amazing read! A great story on magic and witches as well as friendship and family. A beautiful story for mother and daughter, but of course anyone can read it and I do recommend it. The chapter titles were eye catching and interesting. I liked how the author created each character. They were unique and individual with their own sets of skills and talents. The ending was great and it got me a bit teary eyed. Would have been awesome if there was a cure for Antain's face because he</span>
  <span id="freeText17999708540913825445" style="display:none">This book was an amazing read! A great story on magic and witches as well as friendship and family. A beautiful story for mother and daughter, but of course anyone can read it and I do recommend it. The chapter titles were eye catching and interesting. I liked how the author created each character. They were unique and individual with their own sets of skills and talents. The ending was great and it got me a bit teary eyed. Would have been awesome if there was a cure for Antain's face because he's such a sweet guy. I loved how sorrow was spotlight in this book and the weapon to beat it.<br /><br /> This book started with a kid being told a story of an existence of a witch in the woods. Each year, when The Day of Sacrifice arrived, the youngest child in the town has to be sacrificed to a witch. No one knew why. Then the story began with Grand Elder Gherland, told in the third person point of view, who was the leader of the town. He rather enjoyed The Day of Sacrifice and kept a fat secret from the people in town, until his nephew Antain, nearly 13 Elder-in-training, started questioning the process. The second view was Xan, the Witch, more than 500 years old. Every year she arrived at the forest to rescue an infant and brought the baby to a new home. Except this year, Witch Xan took a detour and brought the baby, named her Luna home to be part of her family with Glerk, the swamp monster and Fyrian, the small dragon. The third view was Antain, now nearly 18. He has been faking sick for the past 5 years on The Day of Sacrifice because of what he had witnessed during his first time out. The fourth view was the madwoman at the top of the Tower with her paper birds. Readers will know how each person felt as the story included them like Sister Ignatia, Wyn, Ethyne, etc. The mystery of the town and the witch slowly unravel as the story move forward. <br /><br />The Girl Who Drank the Moon was very well written and a fast paced read! Such an original story unlike any others I have read before, though the beginning reminded me of The Hunger Games where a sacrifice was required from the poor population. The title was explained in the story and it was excellent. I loved the cover of this book! The characters were well developed and I couldn't help but felt for Antain and his wife as well as Glerk, Xan, Fyrian, and Luna. The origami paper birds are a plus! I used to hang my ceiling full of paper birds back in middle and high school. Loved the suspense and mystery and at times a couldn't put down kind of read.<br /><br />xoxo, Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for more details <br /><br />Many thanks to Algonquin Books for Young Readers for the opportunity to read and review. Please be assured that my opinions are honest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17999708540913825445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17124654-zoeereads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17124654-zoeereads?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873569563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5391208640034003004">Oh my goodness what a stubby story. I really loved this book. The cast of characters... ugh, swoon. Xan was so lovely. Fyurein was so loveable (and my fave). Luna was complex and stubborn and relatable. Glurk was so wise. Athene was beautiful and kind. Antane was brave and honest. <br/><br/>The themes in this book really blew me away the most. As a children’s novel, to dig into issues like death, mixed families, sorrow, hope, and love.. that’s a big feat and they were all woven together delicately through</span>
  <span id="freeText5391208640034003004" style="display:none">Oh my goodness what a stubby story. I really loved this book. The cast of characters... ugh, swoon. Xan was so lovely. Fyurein was so loveable (and my fave). Luna was complex and stubborn and relatable. Glurk was so wise. Athene was beautiful and kind. Antane was brave and honest. <br /><br />The themes in this book really blew me away the most. As a children’s novel, to dig into issues like death, mixed families, sorrow, hope, and love.. that’s a big feat and they were all woven together delicately throughout. <br /><br />My only complaint is the repetition of metaphors, and words in general. I can understand that as a middle grade repetition is good, but I started cringing every time I read “she is here” and the word “paper”. <br /><br />All in all this was SO wonderful and I highly recommend that more people read this one! </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1946016736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946016736" />
    <a title="Sarah DiMento" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7883731-sarah-dimento"><img alt="Sarah DiMento" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491621798p2/7883731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946016736?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah DiMento" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah DiMento" href="/user/show/7883731-sarah-dimento">Sarah DiMento</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7883731-sarah-dimento?shelf=love-the-title">love-the-title</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946016736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10749319683121511817">4.5 stars<br/><br/>To be honest, the blurb for this book was TL;DR but I picked it up based on the title and cover alone. That's almost a sure way to be disappointed, I know, but in this case it worked out!<br/><br/>So, what do you get when you take:<br/><br/>-a kind and clever witch<br/>-a poetry reciting swamp monster<br/>-an adorably naive Perfectly Tiny Dragon who believes he's actually a Simply Enormous Dragon<br/>-a girl whose magic cannot be contained<br/><br/>Mix in a volcano, a town swamped with sorrow, add heaping spoonfuls of starlight, m</span>
  <span id="freeText10749319683121511817" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />To be honest, the blurb for this book was TL;DR but I picked it up based on the title and cover alone. That's almost a sure way to be disappointed, I know, but in this case it worked out!<br /><br />So, what do you get when you take:<br /><br />-a kind and clever witch<br />-a poetry reciting swamp monster<br />-an adorably naive Perfectly Tiny Dragon who believes he's actually a Simply Enormous Dragon<br />-a girl whose magic cannot be contained<br /><br />Mix in a volcano, a town swamped with sorrow, add heaping spoonfuls of starlight, moonlight, lyrical writing that ignites the senses, a dreamy fairy tale quality, and, finally, a dash of humor?<br /><br />One of the most enchanting and endearing books I've ever read.<br /><br />The first half of this book was an easy five stars. My only complaint: By the second half, there were moments that felt repetitive, redundant, and a bit wordy, especially for middle grade. It was hard to imagine a fifth grader reading this at times. But then again, the last time I read a middle grade novel was probably when I was actually the target audience for such novels, so what do I know. Highly recommend this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10749319683121511817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ebeq7vW1mElzvo23G3V+h+3mo0aAL9ggUdLSB+C5NJbsP1hA4aswA8NitEA+87GPJ87VQSxbJA9UyVv/jWmCiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9+OITa2InC79+1RqBrXQcfNVfEg0DyJcJsL3zlm2/rhia3rjuZY0ZE0nbZ0jMx95OX0KT5h73nMj2X42NGZIpw==')})
  }

Having been born on Eventide, the unluckiest day for any child to be born, she\'s blamed for all local misfortunes, from hailstorms to heart attacks--and, worst of all, the curse means that Morrigan is doomed to die at midnight on her eleventh birthday.But as Morrigan awaits her fate, a strange and remarkable man named Jupiter North appears. Chased by black-smoke hounds and shadowy hunters on horseback, he whisks her away into the safety of a secret, magical city called Nevermoor.It\'s then that Morrigan discovers Jupiter has chosen her to contend for a place in the city\'s most prestigious organization: the Wundrous Society. In order to join, she must compete in four difficult and dangerous trials against hundreds of other children, each boasting an extraordinary talent that sets them apart - an extraordinary talent that Morrigan insists she does not have. To stay in the safety of Nevermoor for good, Morrigan will need to find a way to pass the tests - or she\'ll have to leave the city to confront her deadly fate.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6352696805136579879">Kelly Barnhill is an author and teacher. She won the World Fantasy Award for her novella <i>The Unlicensed Magician</i>, a Parents Choice Gold Award for <i>Iron Hearted Violet</i>, the Charlotte Huck Honor for <i>The Girl Who Drank the Moon</i>, and has been a finalist for the Minnesota Book Award, the Andre Norton award, and the PEN/USA literary prize. She was also a McKnight Artist's Fellowship recipient in Children</span>
  <span id="freeText6352696805136579879" style="display:none">Kelly Barnhill is an author and teacher. She won the World Fantasy Award for her novella <i>The Unlicensed Magician</i>, a Parents Choice Gold Award for <i>Iron Hearted Violet</i>, the Charlotte Huck Honor for <i>The Girl Who Drank the Moon</i>, and has been a finalist for the Minnesota Book Award, the Andre Norton award, and the PEN/USA literary prize. She was also a McKnight Artist's Fellowship recipient in Children's Literature. She lives in Minneapolis, Minnesota with her three children and husband. You can chat with her on her blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kellybarnhill.com">www.kellybarnhill.com</a></span>
